    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="13123ca3ebb644b79ae7c08b34199b49">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: '94b7dd2c-a32a-4165-a87f-28f089a0f54c'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d78737143" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>Boosting the ultralow temperature (below −30&nbsp;°C) performance of Na-ion hybrid capacitors (SIHCs), which integrate the high energy density of batteries with the high output power and long life of supercapacitors, is critical for the application of advanced electronics in extreme environments. However, their low-temperature performance, especially fast charging capability, is hindered by difficult desolvation and slow pass solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) together with sluggish diffusion within the electrode. Herein, a “single-solute–single-solvent” electrolyte is developed and a through-hole hollow carbon sphere (TH-HCS) is constructed, and it is demonstrated through theoretical calculations and experimental investigations that the weakly solvated structure and high ionic conductivity facilitate the Na<sup>+</sup> transportation at low temperatures, the highly fluorinated SEI facilitates the Na<sup>+</sup> migration, and the through-hole hollow structure alleviates the volume expansion during sodiation, thus ensuring fast kinetics and structural stability. As expected, TH-HCS using this electrolyte exhibits a high specific capacity of 87.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 11&nbsp;000 cycles at 1.0 A g<sup>−1</sup> and −40&nbsp;°C. Coupled with activated carbon, the assembled SIHC displays an energy density of 106.1 and 52.0&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> at 25 and −40&nbsp;°C, respectively, far exceeding the performance of commercial energy storage systems at low temperature.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202301509-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202301509-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>Considering the abundant Na reserve and its worldwide distribution, Na-based energy storage device including Na-ion batteries (SIBs) and Na-metal batteries (SMBs) is a promising choice for electrical vehicles and large-scale stationary energy storage.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0001_R_d78737132e505" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Nat. Energy">1</a>-<a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0004_R_d78737132e505" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Nat. Commun.">4</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To meet the application requirements of high altitudes and cold area as well as defense and space, it is necessary to research and enhance their fast charging and low-temperature (LT) performance (below 0&nbsp;°C). Nevertheless, SIBs face sluggish kinetic challenges arising from larger ionic radius of Na<sup>+</sup> to restrict insertion and extraction of Na<sup>+</sup> from electrode with bulk structure, while Na metal anodes of SMBs are known for poor cycling stability, where large volume change paired with the high reactivity of metallic Na inevitably yields low Coulombic efficiency (CE).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0001_R_d78737132e514" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Nat. Energy">1</a>, <a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0004_R_d78737132e514" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Nat. Commun.">4</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The aforementioned issues severely limit the fast-charging performance of device. Besides, both the capacity retention and operating voltage of SIBs and SMBs are known to suffer severely at LT because the sluggish kinetics and the high melting point (e.g., 10&nbsp;°C for ethylene carbonate (EC)/dimethyl carbonate (DMC) 1:1 by mole) causes the conventional carbonate electrolytes to become more viscous or even freeze, leading to a dramatic decrease in ionic conductivity and an increase in interfacial impedance, resulting in poor LT performance.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0002_R_d78737132e520" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Adv. Energy Mater.">2</a>, <a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0004_R_d78737132e520" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Nat. Commun.">4</a>-<a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0006_R_d78737132e520" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Adv. Sci.">6</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Na-ion hybrid capacitors (SIHCs), which integrate the merits of high power density and long lifetime of supercapacitors with the high energy density of batteries, are expected to avoid the abovementioned problems of SIBs and SMBs at LT and exhibit fast-charging performance. Unfortunately, to date, there are no works of SIHCs that can operate at −30&nbsp;°C and below.</p>
         
         <p>By drawing on studies of LT Li-ion batteries, the main limiting factor of LT performance of SIHCs is also the sluggish Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics, including difficult desolvation, slow transport through solid electrolyte interphase (SEI), and sluggish diffusion within electrode.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0002_R_d78737132e530" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Adv. Energy Mater.">2</a>, <a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0004_R_d78737132e530" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Nat. Commun.">4</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To address this challenge, a common strategy is to use a thermal management system, which has been widely applied in electric vehicles.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0003_R_d78737132e535" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Adv. Mater.">3</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, this inevitably increases the cost and complexity of the entire system, and thus reduces overall energy efficiency. Further enhancement of LT performance by regulating the ontology energy storage system is highly appealed. Current strategy focuses on three aspects. i) Preparation and use of LT resistant electrolytes with high ionic conductivity and easy desolvation structure are the prerequisite.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0003_R_d78737132e541" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Adv. Mater.">3</a>, <a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0004_R_d78737132e541" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Nat. Commun.">4</a>, <a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0007_R_d78737132e541" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> For instance, Wang et&nbsp;al.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0004_R_d78737132e546" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Nat. Commun.">4</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> improved the LT performance of Na-metal battery by using a sodium-trifluoromethanesulfonate (NaOTf)-salt-based LT resistant electrolyte with easy desolvation structure. Similarly, Fan et&nbsp;al.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0008_R_d78737132e551" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Nat. Energy">8</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> achieved a high LT performance by introducing nonpolar solvents to all-fluorinated electrolytes to reduce desolvation energy. These results qualitatively confirm the importance of low desolvation energy for LT properties. ii) Reducing the interface resistance associated with Na<sup>+</sup> transport in SEI is another key to improving fast-charging capability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0009_R_d78737132e559" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Nat. Commun.">9</a>, <a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0010_R_d78737132e559" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">10</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Compared with the cathode side, the interfacial resistance at the anode has been identified as a major barrier.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0009_R_d78737132e564" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Nat. Commun.">9</a>-<a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0011_R_d78737132e564" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">11</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the components of SEI formed in the carbonate electrolyte are unsatisfactory, while the resulting poor mechanical properties will rupture during cycling and subsequently expose new electrode surface, thus causing continuous electrolyte decomposition and resulting in poor cycle life.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0012_R_d78737132e570" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">12</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Besides, the thickened SEI is not conducive to rapid ionic diffusion, limiting the fast-charging capability. Obtaining a SEI with high Na<sup>+</sup> diffusivity and enhanced stability has become a top priority goal. iii) Na<sup>+</sup> storage/diffusion kinetic issues in the interior and/or surface of electrode would also determine its LT properties. Activated carbon (AC) has demonstrated fast kinetic properties as a common cathode electrode for SIHC. For the anode, compared to other conversion or alloy-type electrodes, the carbon-based anode is regarded as one of the best candidates for ion hybrid capacitors.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0013_R_d78737132e579" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Adv. Energy Mater.">13</a>-<a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0015_R_d78737132e579" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - Chem. Eng. J.">15</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Unfortunately, an unsatisfactory rate and cycle properties in existing carbon-based anodes fail to match the kinetics of AC. Designing novel carbon materials with unique structures is considered as one of the relatively effective means. For instance, the porous structure can alleviate the volume expansion during de/sodiation and shorten the Na<sup>+</sup> migration distance, and, as a result, enhance rate capability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0003_R_d78737132e587" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Adv. Mater.">3</a>, <a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0013_R_d78737132e587" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Adv. Energy Mater.">13</a>, <a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0016_R_d78737132e587" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Nevertheless, improving cycle life and rate property by a single structure modulation without sacrificing other critical properties is technically nontrivial. For example, abundant porous structure causes severe side reactions in the first cycle, resulting in low initial CE (ICE).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0010_R_d78737132e592" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">10</a>, <a href="#aenm202301509-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202301509-bib-0012_R_d78737132e592" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">12</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Such electrodes often require multiple cycles to form a stable SEI. How to improve the comprehensive performance of the anode needs to be carefully considered. Overall, improving the LT performance of SIHCs requires consideration of various aspects, such as a suitable electrolyte and properly designed anode material with unique structures.</p>
         
         <p>Here, a novel “single-salt–single-solvent” ether LT resistant electrolyte (1.0&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaOTf–diethylene glycol dimethyl ether (DEGDME)) was developed and simultaneously a unique through-hole hollow carbon sphere (TH-HCS) was constructed to achieve the ultimate goal described above (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202301509-fig-0001">1</a>). Compared with the conventional 1.0&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaPF<sub>6</sub>–EC/DMC, NaOTf salt facilitated the formation of thinner SEI and reversible storage of Na<sup>+</sup>, while DEGDME solvent favored the construction of a smooth and compact inorganic-rich SEI. Importantly, the preferred electrolyte with high electron affinity and high-polarity of the ─CF<sub>3</sub> groups showed low desolvation structure, improving the Na<sup>+</sup> migration kinetics and avoiding the cointercalation of Na<sup>+</sup>–solvent. Meanwhile, through-hole hollow structure alleviated the volume expansion during sodiation and promoted electrolyte permeation, ensuring fast kinetics at LT. Benefiting from the weakly solvated electrolyte and optimized anode structure, TH-HCS exhibited a high ICE of 84.5% at 25&nbsp;°C, a high specific capacity of 58.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 1.0 A g<sup>−1</sup> and −60&nbsp;°C, and long-cycling life of 87.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> even after 11&nbsp;000 cycles at 1.0 A g<sup>−1</sup> and −40&nbsp;°C. As expected, TH-HCS assembled with AC to construct a SIHC exhibited a high energy density of 106.1 and 52.0&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> at 25 and −40&nbsp;°C, respectively. These powerful results provide a novel standpoint for building LT storage devices with superior performance and further understanding of practical applications.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="aenm202301509-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/5d822ce3-5bf4-4a17-8ead-702cdf8b2d14/aenm202301509-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/5d822ce3-5bf4-4a17-8ead-702cdf8b2d14/aenm202301509-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/341d1485-7789-4cf8-8bb3-6a62f754cb07/aenm202301509-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/5d822ce3-5bf4-4a17-8ead-702cdf8b2d14/aenm202301509-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
